      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Country in Central Africa
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>; for similarly named entities, see <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Republic of the Congo (disambiguation)">Republic of the Congo (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "DRC" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/DRC_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="DRC (disambiguation)">DRC (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

      <p>The <b>Democratic Republic of the Congo</b> (<b>DRC</b>) (<span style="font-size:85%;"><span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-DRC-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ec/En-DRC-pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="En-DRC-pronunciation.ogg">pronunciation</a></span>&nbsp;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:En-DRC-pronunciation.ogg" title="File:En-DRC-pronunciation.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span></span> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">République démocratique du Congo (RDC)</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[kɔ̃ɡo]</a></span>), also known as <b>Congo-Kinshasa</b>, <b>DR Congo</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">RD Congo</i>), <b>the DROC</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-DROC_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DROC-9">[8]</a></sup> <b>the DRC</b>, or simply either <b>Congo</b> or <b>the Congo</b>, and historically <b><a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a></b>, is a country in <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>. It is, by area, the largest country in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>, the second-largest in all of Africa (after <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">11th-largest in the world</a>. With a population of around 105 million, the Democratic Republic of the Congo is the most populous <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_where_French_is_an_official_language" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries where French is an official language">officially Francophone country</a> in the world, as well as the 4th-most populous country in Africa (after <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>) and the 15th-most populous country in the world. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa">COMESA</a>. Since 2015, the Eastern DR Congo has been the site of an <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">ongoing military conflict in Kivu</a>. </p>
      <p>Centered on the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Basin" title="Congo Basin">Congo Basin</a>, the territory of the DRC was first inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Central_African_foragers" class="mw-redirect" title="Central African foragers">Central African foragers</a> around 90,000 years ago and was reached by the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a> about 3,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> In the west, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a> ruled around the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> from the 14th to 19th centuries. In the northeast, center and east, the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Zande_people" title="Zande people">Azande</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Luba" title="Kingdom of Luba">Luba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Lunda" title="Kingdom of Lunda">Lunda</a> ruled from the 16th and 17th centuries to the 19th century. </p>
      <p>In the 1870s, just before the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>, European <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_the_Congo_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Exploration of the Congo Basin">exploration of the Congo Basin</a> was carried out, first led by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Morton_Stanley" title="Henry Morton Stanley">Henry Morton Stanley</a> under the sponsorship of <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">Leopold II of Belgium</a>. Leopold formally acquired rights to the Congo territory at the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a> in 1885 and declared the land his private property, naming it the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>. During the Free State, his <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial</a> military unit, the <i><a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a>,</i> forced the local population to produce <a href="/wiki/Natural_rubber" title="Natural rubber">rubber</a>. From 1885 to 1908, millions of Congolese people died as a consequence of <a href="/wiki/Atrocities_in_the_Congo_Free_State" title="Atrocities in the Congo Free State">disease and exploitation</a>. In 1908, Leopold, despite his initial reluctance, <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium#Relinquishment_of_the_Congo" title="Leopold II of Belgium">ceded</a> the so-called Free State to <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, thus it became known as the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a>. </p>
      <p>Congo achieved independence from Belgium on 30 June 1960 under the name <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Republic of the Congo</a>. <a href="/wiki/Congolese_nationalism_(Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo)" title="Congolese nationalism (Democratic Republic of the Congo)">Congolese nationalist</a> <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a> was <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo_general_election,_1960" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian Congo general election, 1960">elected</a> the first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Prime Minister</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu" title="Joseph Kasa-Vubu">Joseph Kasa-Vubu</a> became the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="President of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">President</a>. Conflict arose over the administration of the territory, which became known as the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">Congo Crisis</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Provinces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">provinces</a> of <a href="/wiki/State_of_Katanga" title="State of Katanga">Katanga</a>, under <a href="/wiki/Mo%C3%AFse_Tshombe" title="Moïse Tshombe">Moïse Tshombe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Kasai" title="South Kasai">South Kasai</a> attempted to secede. After the UN and Western governments refused his requests for aid and Lumumba stated that he was open to any country, including the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, for assistance in the crisis, the US and Belgium became wary and oversaw his removal from office by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu" title="Joseph Kasa-Vubu">Kasa-Vubu</a> on 5 September and ultimate execution by Belgian-led Katangese troops on 17 January 1961. </p>
      <p>On 25 November 1965, Army Chief of Staff Joseph-Désiré Mobutu, who later renamed himself <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a>, officially came into power through a <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis#Second_Mobutu_coup_d'état" title="Congo Crisis">coup d'état</a>. In 1971, he renamed the country <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>. The country was run as a <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorial</a> <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a>, with his <a href="/wiki/Popular_Movement_of_the_Revolution" title="Popular Movement of the Revolution">Popular Movement of the Revolution</a> as the sole legal party. Mobutu's government received considerable support from the United States, due to its anti-communist stance during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. By the early 1990s, Mobutu's government began to weaken. Destabilisation in the east resulting from the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a> and disenfranchisement among the eastern <a href="/wiki/Banyamulenge" title="Banyamulenge">Banyamulenge</a> (Congolese Rwandans of the Tutsi tribe) population led to a 1996 invasion led by <a href="/wiki/Tutsi" title="Tutsi">Tutsi</a> <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Patriotic_Front" title="Rwandan Patriotic Front">FPR</a>-ruled Rwanda, which began the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First Congo War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-4">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 17 May 1997, <a href="/wiki/Laurent-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Kabila" title="Laurent-Désiré Kabila">Laurent-Désiré Kabila</a>, a leader of Tutsi forces from the province of <a href="/wiki/South_Kivu" title="South Kivu">South Kivu</a>, became President after Mobutu fled to <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, reverting the country's name to the Democratic Republic of the Congo. Tensions between President Kabila and the Rwandan and Tutsi presence in the country led to the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a> from 1998 to 2003. Ultimately, nine African countries and around twenty armed groups became involved in the war,<sup id="cite_ref-Bowers2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bowers2-11">[10]</a></sup> which resulted in the deaths of 5.4&nbsp;million people.<sup id="cite_ref-IRC2007fullreport_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRC2007fullreport-12">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_deadliest_war_in_the_world_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_deadliest_war_in_the_world-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IRC2007Facts_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRC2007Facts-15">[14]</a></sup> The two wars devastated the country. President Laurent-Désiré Kabila was assassinated by one of his bodyguards on 16 January 2001 and was succeeded eight days later by his son <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> under whom <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Human rights in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">human rights in the country</a> remained poor and included frequent abuses such as <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">forced disappearances</a>, torture, arbitrary imprisonment and restrictions on civil liberties according to NGOs.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/2018_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_general_election" title="2018 Democratic Republic of the Congo general election">2018 general election</a>, Kabila was succeeded as president by <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi" title="Félix Tshisekedi">Félix Tshisekedi</a> in the country's first <a href="/wiki/Peaceful_transition_of_power" title="Peaceful transition of power">peaceful transition of power</a> since independence, who has served as president since.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo is extremely rich in <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a> but has suffered from <a href="/wiki/Fragile_state" title="Fragile state">political instability</a>, a lack of infrastructure, corruption, and centuries of both commercial and colonial extraction and exploitation with little widespread development. Besides the capital <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>, the two next largest cities, <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mbuji-Mayi" title="Mbuji-Mayi">Mbuji-Mayi</a> are both mining communities. The DRC's largest export is raw minerals, with China accepting over 50% of its exports in 2012. In 2019, DR Congo's level of human development was ranked 175th out of 189 countries by the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHDR_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHDR-8">[7]</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, around 600,000 Congolese have fled to neighbouring countries from conflicts in the centre and east of the DRC.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> Two million children risk starvation, and the fighting has displaced 4.5&nbsp;million people.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo people</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo is named after the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>, which flows throughout the country. The Congo River is the world's deepest river and the world's second-largest river <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_by_discharge" title="List of rivers by discharge">by discharge</a>. The <i>Comité d'études du haut Congo</i> ("Committee for the Study of the Upper Congo"), established by <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">King Leopold II of Belgium</a> in 1876, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_the_Congo" title="International Association of the Congo">International Association of the Congo</a>, established by him in 1879, were also named after the river.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Congo River itself was named by early European sailors after the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> inhabitants, the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo people</a>, when they encountered them in the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> The word <i>Kongo</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_language" title="Kongo language">Kongo language</a> (also called <i>Kikongo</i>). According to American writer Samuel Henry Nelson: "It is probable that the word 'Kongo' itself implies a public gathering and that it is based on the root <i>konga</i>, 'to gather' (trans[itive])."<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> The modern name of the Kongo people, <i>Bakongo</i> was introduced in the early 20th century. </p>
      <p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo has been known in the past as, in chronological order, the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Republic of the Congo-Léopoldville</a>, the Democratic Republic of the Congo and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Zaire" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Zaire">Republic of Zaire</a>, before returning to its current name the Democratic Republic of the Congo.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-4">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the time of independence, the country was named the Republic of the Congo-Léopoldville to distinguish it from its neighbour the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo-Brazzaville</a>. With the promulgation of the <a href="/wiki/Luluabourg_Constitution" title="Luluabourg Constitution">Luluabourg Constitution</a> on 1 August 1964, the country became the DRC, but was renamed to <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a> (a past name for the Congo River) on 27 October 1971 by President <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a> as part of his <i><a href="/wiki/Authenticit%C3%A9_(Zaire)" title="Authenticité (Zaire)">Authenticité</a></i> initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-kisanganibobb_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kisanganibobb-25">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The word <i>Zaire</i> is from a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> adaptation of a <a href="/wiki/Kongo_language" title="Kongo language">Kikongo</a> word <i>nzadi</i> ("river"), a truncation of <i>nzadi o nzere</i> ("river swallowing rivers").<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> The river was known as <i>Zaire</i> during the 16th and 17th centuries; <i>Congo</i> seems to have replaced <i>Zaire</i> gradually in English usage during the 18th century, and <i>Congo</i> is the preferred English name in 19th-century literature, although references to <i>Zaire</i> as the name used by the natives (i.e. derived from Portuguese usage) remained common.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1992, the Sovereign National Conference voted to change the name of the country to the "Democratic Republic of the Congo", but the change was not made.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> The country's name was later restored by President <a href="/wiki/Laurent-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Kabila" title="Laurent-Désiré Kabila">Laurent-Désiré Kabila</a> when he overthrew Mobutu in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> To distinguish it from the neighboring Republic of the Congo, it is sometimes referred to as <i>Congo (Kinshasa)</i> or <i>Congo-Kinshasa</i>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="History of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">History of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
