      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Early_Congolese_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Congolese history">Early Congolese history</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The geographical area now known as the Democratic Republic of the Congo was populated as early as 90,000 years ago, as shown by the 1988 discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Semliki_harpoon" title="Semliki harpoon">Semliki harpoon</a> at <a href="/wiki/Katanda_Territory" title="Katanda Territory">Katanda</a>, one of the oldest barbed harpoons ever found, believed to have been used to catch <a href="/wiki/Bagrus" title="Bagrus">giant river catfish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> reached Central Africa at some point during the first millennium BC, then gradually started to expand southward. Their propagation was accelerated by the adoption of <a href="/wiki/Pastoralism" title="Pastoralism">pastoralism</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> techniques. The people living in the south and southwest were <a href="/wiki/Central_African_foragers" class="mw-redirect" title="Central African foragers">foraging</a> groups, whose technology involved only minimal use of metal technologies. The development of metal tools during this time period revolutionized agriculture. This led to the displacement of the hunter-gatherer groups in the east and southeast. The final wave of the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a> was complete by the 10th century, followed by the establishment of the Bantu kingdoms, whose rising populations soon made possible intricate local, regional and foreign commercial networks that traded mostly in slaves, salt, iron and copper. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Congo_Free_State_.281877.E2.80.931908.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Congo_Free_State_(1877–1908)">Congo Free State (1877–1908)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Congo Free State (1877–1908)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonisation of the Congo">Colonisation of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Atrocities_in_the_Congo_Free_State" title="Atrocities in the Congo Free State">Atrocities in the Congo Free State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Congo_Arab_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Congo Arab war">Congo Arab war</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dhanis_Expedition.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Dhanis_Expedition.JPG/170px-Dhanis_Expedition.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Dhanis_Expedition.JPG/255px-Dhanis_Expedition.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Dhanis_Expedition.JPG/340px-Dhanis_Expedition.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2136" data-file-height="2844"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dhanis_Expedition.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A contemporary depiction of a Belgian expedition during the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Arab_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Congo Arab war">Congo Arab war</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg/220px-Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg/330px-Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg/440px-Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1343" data-file-height="947"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>View of <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Leopoldville</a> Station and Port in 1884
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian exploration</a> and administration took place from the 1870s until the 1920s. It was first led by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Henry_Morton_Stanley" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Henry Morton Stanley">Sir Henry Morton Stanley</a>, who undertook his explorations under the sponsorship of <a href="/wiki/King_Leopold_II_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="King Leopold II of Belgium">King Leopold II of Belgium</a>. The eastern regions of the precolonial Congo were heavily disrupted by constant <a href="/wiki/Slave_raiding" title="Slave raiding">slave raiding</a>, mainly from Arab–Swahili <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">slave traders</a> such as the infamous <a href="/wiki/Tippu_Tip" title="Tippu Tip">Tippu Tip</a>, who was well known to Stanley.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Leopold had designs on what was to become the Congo as a colony.<sup id="cite_ref-cfskeyes_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfskeyes-35">[34]</a></sup> In a succession of negotiations, Leopold, professing humanitarian objectives in his capacity as chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Front_organization" title="Front organization">front organization</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Association_Internationale_Africaine" class="mw-redirect" title="Association Internationale Africaine">Association Internationale Africaine</a></i>, actually played one European rival against another.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Leopold formally acquired rights to the Congo territory at the <a href="/wiki/Conference_of_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Conference of Berlin">Conference of Berlin</a> in 1885 and made the land his private property. He named it the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cfskeyes_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfskeyes-35">[34]</a></sup> Leopold's regime began various infrastructure projects, such as the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Matadi%E2%80%93Kinshasa_Railway" title="Matadi–Kinshasa Railway">railway that ran from the coast to the capital</a> of Leopoldville (now Kinshasa), which took eight years to complete. Nearly all such infrastructure projects were aimed at making it easier to increase the assets which Leopold and his associates could extract from the colony.<sup id="cite_ref-b1_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b1-36">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the Free State, colonists coerced the local population into producing <a href="/wiki/Rubber" class="mw-redirect" title="Rubber">rubber</a>, for which the spread of automobiles and development of rubber tires created a growing international market. Rubber sales made a fortune for Leopold, who built several buildings in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ostend" title="Ostend">Ostend</a> to honor himself and his country. To enforce the rubber quotas, the army, the <i><a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a></i>, was called in and made the practice of cutting off the limbs of the natives a matter of policy.<sup id="cite_ref-google748_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google748-37">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the period of 1885–1908, millions of Congolese died as a consequence of exploitation and disease. In some areas the population declined dramatically&nbsp;– it has been estimated that <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">sleeping sickness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> killed nearly half the population in the areas surrounding the lower Congo River.<sup id="cite_ref-google748_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google748-37">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>News of the abuses began to circulate. In 1904, the British consul at Boma in the Congo, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Casement" title="Roger Casement">Roger Casement</a>, was instructed by the British government to investigate. His report, called the <a href="/wiki/Casement_Report" title="Casement Report">Casement Report</a>, confirmed the accusations of humanitarian abuses. The Belgian Parliament forced Leopold II to set up an independent commission of inquiry. Its findings confirmed Casement's report of abuses, concluding that the population of the Congo had been "reduced by half" during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-b1_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b1-36">[35]</a></sup> Determining precisely how many people died is impossible, as no accurate records exist. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Belgian_Congo_.281908.E2.80.931960.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgian_Congo_(1908–1960)">Belgian Congo (1908–1960)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Belgian Congo (1908–1960)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bugidi,_the_mission_engineer,_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy,_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg/170px-Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg/255px-Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg/340px-Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg 2x" data-file-width="464" data-file-height="760"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bugidi,_the_mission_engineer,_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy,_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>1908 photograph of a married <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> couple.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1908, the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian parliament">Belgian parliament</a>, in spite of initial reluctance, bowed to international pressure (especially from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>) and took over the Free State from <a href="/wiki/King_Leopold_II" class="mw-redirect" title="King Leopold II">King Leopold II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 18 October 1908, the Belgian parliament voted in favour of annexing the Congo as a Belgian <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a>. Executive power went to the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_the_Colonies_(Belgium)" title="Minister of the Colonies (Belgium)">Belgian minister of colonial affairs</a>, assisted by a Colonial Council (Conseil Colonial) (both located in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>). The Belgian parliament exercised legislative authority over the Belgian Congo. In 1923 the colonial capital moved from Boma to <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9opoldville" class="mw-redirect" title="Léopoldville">Léopoldville</a>, some 300 kilometres (190&nbsp;mi) further upstream into the interior.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-39">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The transition from the Congo Free State to the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a> was a break but it also featured a large degree of continuity. The last Governor-general of the Congo Free State, Baron <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9ophile_Wahis" title="Théophile Wahis">Théophile Wahis</a>, remained in office in the Belgian Congo and the majority of Leopold II's administration with him.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> Opening up the Congo and its natural and mineral riches to the Belgian economy remained the main motive for colonial expansion&nbsp;– however, other priorities, such as healthcare and basic education, slowly gained in importance. </p>
      <p> Colonial administrators ruled the territory and a dual legal system existed (a system of European courts and another one of indigenous courts, <i>tribunaux indigènes</i>). Indigenous courts had only limited powers and remained under the firm control of the colonial administration. </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg/170px-Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg/255px-Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg/340px-Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg 2x" data-file-width="972" data-file-height="974"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a></i> soldiers in the Belgian Congo in 1918. At its peak, the Force Publique had around 19,000 Congolese soldiers, led by 420 Belgian officers.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p> Records show that in 1936, 728 Belgian administrators ran the colony.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Belgian authorities permitted no political activity in the Congo whatsoever,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a></i>, a locally-recruited army under Belgian command, put down any attempts at rebellion. </p>
      <p>The Belgian population of the colony increased from 1,928 in 1910 to nearly 89,000 in 1959.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The Belgian Congo was directly involved in the two world wars. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> (1914–1918), an initial stand-off between the <i>Force Publique</i> and the German colonial army in <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German East Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tanganyika_(territory)" title="Tanganyika (territory)">Tanganyika</a>) turned into open warfare with a joint Anglo-Belgian-Portuguese invasion of German colonial territory in 1916 and 1917 during the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_I)" class="mw-redirect" title="East African Campaign (World War I)">East African Campaign</a>. The <i>Force Publique</i> gained a notable victory when it marched into <a href="/wiki/Tabora" title="Tabora">Tabora</a> in September 1916 under the command of General <a href="/wiki/Charles_Tombeur" title="Charles Tombeur">Charles Tombeur</a> after heavy fighting. </p>
      <p>After 1918, Belgium was rewarded for the participation of the <i>Force Publique</i> in the East African campaign with a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> mandate over the previously German colony of <a href="/wiki/Ruanda-Urundi" title="Ruanda-Urundi">Ruanda-Urundi</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the Belgian Congo provided a crucial source of income for the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_government_in_exile" title="Belgian government in exile">Belgian government-in-exile</a> in London, and the <i>Force Publique</i> again participated in Allied campaigns in Africa. Belgian Congolese forces under the command of Belgian officers notably fought against the Italian colonial army in Ethiopia in <a href="/wiki/Asosa" title="Asosa">Asosa</a>, Bortaï<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sa%C3%AFo" title="Siege of Saïo">Saïo</a> under Major-General <a href="/wiki/Auguste-Eduard_Gilliaert" class="mw-redirect" title="Auguste-Eduard Gilliaert">Auguste-Eduard Gilliaert</a> during the second <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="East African Campaign (World War II)">East African Campaign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WP_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-43">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_and_political_crisis_.281960.E2.80.931965.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_political_crisis_(1960–1965)">Independence and political crisis (1960–1965)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence and political crisis (1960–1965)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">Congo Crisis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png/170px-Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png/255px-Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png 2x" data-file-width="293" data-file-height="343"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The leader of <a href="/wiki/ABAKO" title="ABAKO">ABAKO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu" title="Joseph Kasa-Vubu">Joseph Kasa-Vubu</a>, first democratically elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="President of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">President</a> of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Congo-Léopoldville</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/220px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/330px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/440px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="467" data-file-height="424"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a>, first democratically elected <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Prime Minister</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Congo-Léopoldville</a>, was murdered by Belgian-supported <a href="/wiki/State_of_Katanga" title="State of Katanga">Katangan separatists</a> in 1961
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In May 1960, a growing nationalist movement, the <a href="/wiki/Mouvement_National_Congolais" title="Mouvement National Congolais">Mouvement National Congolais</a> (MNC) led by <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo_general_election,_1960" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian Congo general election, 1960">parliamentary elections</a>. Patrice Lumumba thus became the first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, then known as the Republic of the Congo, on 24 June 1960. The parliament elected <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kasavubu" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Kasavubu">Joseph Kasavubu</a> as <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="President of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">President</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_des_Bakongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance des Bakongo">Alliance des Bakongo</a> (ABAKO) party. Other parties that emerged included the <a href="/wiki/Parti_Solidaire_Africain" title="Parti Solidaire Africain">Parti Solidaire Africain</a> (PSA) led by <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Gizenga" title="Antoine Gizenga">Antoine Gizenga</a>, and the Parti National du Peuple (PNP) led by Albert Delvaux and <a href="/wiki/Laurent_Mbariko" title="Laurent Mbariko">Laurent Mbariko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Belgian Congo achieved independence on 30 June 1960 under the name "République du Congo" ("Republic of Congo" or "Republic of the Congo" in English). As the neighboring French colony of <a href="/wiki/Middle_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Congo">Middle Congo</a> (Moyen Congo) also chose the name "<a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Congo">Republic of Congo</a>" upon achieving its independence, the two countries were more commonly known as "Congo-Léopoldville" and "Congo-Brazzaville", after their capital cities. </p>
      <p>Shortly after independence the Force Publique mutinied, and on 11 July the <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">province of Katanga</a> (led by <a href="/wiki/Mo%C3%AFse_Tshombe" title="Moïse Tshombe">Moïse Tshombe</a>) and <a href="/wiki/South_Kasai" title="South Kasai">South Kasai</a> engaged in secessionist struggles against the new leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> Most of the 100,000 Europeans who had remained behind after independence fled the country,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> opening the way for Congolese to replace the European military and administrative elite.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> On 5 September 1960, Kasavubu dismissed Lumumba from office. Lumumba declared Kasavubu's action unconstitutional and <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">a crisis</a> between the two leaders developed.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Events set in motion by the U.S. and Belgium on 14 September removed Lumumba from office with forces loyal to <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Mobutu" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Mobutu">Joseph Mobutu</a>. On 17 January 1961, he was handed over to Katangan authorities and executed by Belgian-led Katangese troops.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> An investigation by the Belgium's Parliament in 2001 found Belgium "morally responsible" for the murder of Lumumba, and the country has since officially apologised for its role in his death.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Amidst widespread confusion and chaos, a temporary government was led by technicians (the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Commissioners-General" title="College of Commissioners-General">Collège des commissaires généraux</a>). The secession ended in January 1963 with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Operation_in_the_Congo" title="United Nations Operation in the Congo">assistance of UN forces</a>. Several short-lived governments, of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Ileo" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Ileo">Joseph Ileo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyrille_Adoula" title="Cyrille Adoula">Cyrille Adoula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moise_Kapenda_Tshombe" class="mw-redirect" title="Moise Kapenda Tshombe">Moise Kapenda Tshombe</a>, took over in quick succession. </p>
      <p>Lumumba had previously appointed Joseph Mobutu chief of staff of the new Congo army, <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of the Democratic Republic of Congo">Armée Nationale Congolaise</a> (ANC).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Taking advantage of the leadership crisis between Kasavubu and Tshombe, Mobutu garnered enough support within the army to launch a coup. With financial support from the United States and Belgium, Mobutu paid his soldiers privately.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The aversion of Western powers to communism and leftist ideology influenced their decision to finance Mobutu's quest to neutralize Kasavubu and Lumumba in a coup by proxy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)_constitutional_referendum,_1964" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville) constitutional referendum, 1964">constitutional referendum</a> the year before Mobutu's coup of 1965 resulted in the country's official name being changed to the "Democratic Republic of the Congo."<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-4">[3]</a></sup> In 1971 Mobutu changed the name again, this time to "Republic of Zaire".<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-52">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kisanganibobb_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kisanganibobb-25">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Mobutu_and_Zaire_.281965.E2.80.931997.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobutu_and_Zaire_(1965–1997)">Mobutu and Zaire (1965–1997)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mobutu and Zaire (1965–1997)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mobutu_Nixon.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mobutu_Nixon.gif/220px-Mobutu_Nixon.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mobutu_Nixon.gif/330px-Mobutu_Nixon.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mobutu_Nixon.gif/440px-Mobutu_Nixon.gif 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="387"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mobutu_Nixon.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a> and Richard Nixon in Washington, D.C., 1973.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The new president had the staunch support of the United States because of his <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">opposition</a> to Communism; the US believed that his administration would serve as an effective counter to communist movements in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Single-party_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Single-party system">single-party system</a> was established, and Mobutu declared himself <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Head of state of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">head of state</a>. He periodically held elections in which he was the only candidate. Although relative peace and stability were achieved, Mobutu's government was guilty of severe <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_violations" class="mw-redirect" title="Human rights violations">human rights violations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_repression" title="Political repression">political repression</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_personality" title="Cult of personality">cult of personality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Zaire" class="mw-redirect" title="Corruption in Zaire">corruption</a>. </p>
      <p>By late 1967 Mobutu had successfully neutralized his political opponents and rivals, either through co-opting them into his regime, arresting them, or rendering them otherwise politically impotent.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201358_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201358-54">[53]</a></sup> Throughout the late 1960s, Mobutu continued to shuffle his governments and cycle officials in and out of the office to maintain control. Kasa-Vubu's death in April 1969 ensured that no person with First Republic credentials could challenge his rule.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201361–62_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201361–62-55">[54]</a></sup> By the early 1970s, Mobutu was attempting to assert Zaire as a leading African nation. He traveled frequently across the continent while the government became more vocal about African issues, particularly those relating to the southern region. Zaire established semi-clientelist relationships with several smaller African states, especially Burundi, Chad, and Togo.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201364_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201364-56">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Corruption became so common the term "<i>le mal Zairois</i>" or "Zairian Sickness",<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> meaning gross corruption, theft and mismanagement, was coined, reportedly by Mobutu himself.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201374_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201374-58">[57]</a></sup> International aid, most often in the form of loans, enriched Mobutu while he allowed national infrastructure such as roads to deteriorate to as little as one-quarter of what had existed in 1960. Zaire became a <a href="/wiki/Kleptocracy" title="Kleptocracy">kleptocracy</a> as Mobutu and his associates <a href="/wiki/Embezzlement" title="Embezzlement">embezzled</a> government funds. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg/220px-Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg/330px-Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg/440px-Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1740" data-file-height="1664"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mobutu with the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Bernhard_of_Lippe-Biesterfeld" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernhard of Lippe-Biesterfeld">Prince Bernhard</a> in Kinshasa in 1973
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In a campaign to identify himself with African nationalism, starting on 1 June 1966, Mobutu renamed the nation's cities: Léopoldville became <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a> (the country was now Congo-Kinshasa), Stanleyville became <a href="/wiki/Kisangani" title="Kisangani">Kisangani</a>, Elisabethville became <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a>, and Coquilhatville became <a href="/wiki/Mbandaka" title="Mbandaka">Mbandaka</a>. This renaming campaign was completed in the 1970s. </p>
      <p>In 1971, Mobutu renamed the country the <i>Republic of Zaire</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-kisanganibobb_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kisanganibobb-25">[24]</a></sup> its fourth name change in eleven years and its sixth overall. The <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> was renamed the Zaire River. </p>
      <p>During the 1970s and 1980s, he was invited to visit the United States on several occasions, meeting with U.S. Presidents <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> U.S. relations with Mobutu cooled, as he was no longer deemed necessary as a <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> ally. Opponents within Zaire stepped up demands for reform. This atmosphere contributed to Mobutu's declaring the Third Republic in 1990, whose constitution was supposed to pave the way for democratic reform. The reforms turned out to be largely cosmetic. Mobutu continued in power until armed forces forced him to flee in 1997. "From 1990 to 1993, the United States facilitated Mobutu's attempts to hijack political change", one academic wrote, and "also assisted the rebellion of Laurent-Desire Kabila that overthrew the Mobutu regime."<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Continental_and_civil_wars_.281996.E2.80.932007.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Continental_and_civil_wars_(1996–2007)">Continental and civil wars (1996–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Continental and civil wars (1996–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First Congo War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">Kivu conflict</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ituri_conflict" title="Ituri conflict">Ituri conflict</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png/220px-Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png/330px-Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png/440px-Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png 2x" data-file-width="1526" data-file-height="1444"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Belligerents of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>By 1996, following the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Civil_War" title="Rwandan Civil War">Rwandan Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">genocide</a> and the ascension of a <a href="/wiki/Tutsi" title="Tutsi">Tutsi</a>-led government in Rwanda, Rwandan <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">Hutu</a> militia forces (<a href="/wiki/Interahamwe" title="Interahamwe">Interahamwe</a>) fled to eastern Zaire and used refugee camps as a base for incursions against Rwanda. They allied with the Zairian Armed Forces (FAZ) to launch a campaign against Congolese ethnic Tutsis in eastern Zaire.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A coalition of Rwandan and Ugandan armies invaded Zaire to overthrow the government of Mobutu, and ultimately to control the mineral resources of Zaire,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> launching the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First Congo War</a>. The coalition allied with some opposition figures, led by <a href="/wiki/Laurent-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Kabila" title="Laurent-Désiré Kabila">Laurent-Désiré Kabila</a>, becoming the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Democratic_Forces_for_the_Liberation_of_Congo" title="Alliance of Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Congo">Alliance of Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Congo</a> (AFDL). In 1997 Mobutu fled and Kabila marched into Kinshasa, named himself president, and reverted the name of the country to the Democratic Republic of the Congo. </p>
      <p>Kabila later requested that foreign military forces return to their own countries. He had concerns that the Rwandan officers running his army were plotting to give the presidency to a Tutsi who would report directly to <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>n president, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kagame" title="Paul Kagame">Paul Kagame</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Rwandan troops retreated to Goma and launched a new <a href="/wiki/Tutsi" title="Tutsi">Tutsi</a>-led rebel military movement called the <a href="/wiki/Rassemblement_Congolais_pour_la_Democratie" class="mw-redirect" title="Rassemblement Congolais pour la Democratie">Rassemblement Congolais pour la Democratie</a> (RCD) to fight Kabila, while Uganda instigated the creation of new rebel movement called the <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Movement for the Liberation of Congo">Movement for the Liberation of Congo</a> (MLC), led by Congolese warlord <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Bemba" title="Jean-Pierre Bemba">Jean-Pierre Bemba</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The two rebel movements, along with Rwandan and Ugandan troops, started the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a> by attacking the DRC army in 1998. Angolan, Zimbabwean, and Namibian militaries entered the hostilities on the side of the government. </p>
      <p>Kabila was assassinated in 2001. His son <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> succeeded him and called for multilateral peace talks. UN peacekeepers, <a href="/wiki/MONUC" class="mw-redirect" title="MONUC">MONUC</a>, now known as MONUSCO, arrived in April 2001. In 2002 and 2003 Bemba intervened in the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> on behalf of its former president, <a href="/wiki/Ange-F%C3%A9lix_Patass%C3%A9" title="Ange-Félix Patassé">Ange-Félix Patassé</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> Talks led to a peace accord under which Kabila would share power with former rebels. By June 2003 all foreign armies except those of Rwanda had pulled out of Congo. A <a href="/wiki/Transitional_Government_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Transitional Government of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">transitional government</a> was set up until after the election. A constitution was approved by voters, and on 30 July 2006 DRC held its <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_general_election,_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo general election, 2006">first multi-party elections</a>. An election-result dispute between Kabila and Jean-Pierre Bemba turned into an all-out battle between their supporters in the streets of Kinshasa. MONUC took control of the city. A new election took place in October 2006, which Kabila won, and in December 2006 he was sworn in as President. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg/220px-Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg/330px-Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg/440px-Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Refugees in the Congo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span id="Continued_Conflicts_.282008.E2.80.932018.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_Conflicts_(2008–2018)">Continued Conflicts (2008–2018)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Continued Conflicts (2008–2018)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kivu_conflict">Kivu conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Kivu conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kivu_Conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Kivu Conflict">Kivu Conflict</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Laurent_Nkunda" title="Laurent Nkunda">Laurent Nkunda</a>, a member of <a href="/wiki/RCD-Goma" class="mw-redirect" title="RCD-Goma">RCD-Goma</a>, an RCD branch integrated to the army, defected along with troops loyal to him and formed the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_for_the_Defence_of_the_People" title="National Congress for the Defence of the People">National Congress for the Defence of the People</a> (CNDP), which began an armed rebellion against the government, starting the <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">Kivu conflict</a>. They were believed<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (May 2015)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to be again backed by Rwanda as a way to tackle the <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">Hutu</a> group, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Forces_for_the_Liberation_of_Rwanda" title="Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Rwanda">Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Rwanda</a> (FDLR). In March 2009, after a deal between the DRC and Rwanda, Rwandan troops entered the DRC and arrested Nkunda and were allowed to pursue FDLR militants. The CNDP signed a peace treaty with the government in which it agreed to become a political party and to have its soldiers integrated into the national army in exchange for the release of its imprisoned members.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> In 2012 <a href="/wiki/Bosco_Ntaganda" title="Bosco Ntaganda">Bosco Ntaganda</a>, the leader of the CNDP, and troops loyal to him, mutinied and formed the rebel military <a href="/wiki/March_23_Movement" title="March 23 Movement">March 23 Movement</a>, claiming the government violated the treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the resulting <a href="/wiki/M23_rebellion" title="M23 rebellion">M23 rebellion</a>, M23 briefly captured the provincial capital of <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a> in November 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> Neighboring countries, particularly Rwanda, have been accused of arming rebels groups and using them as proxies to gain control of the resource-rich country, an accusation they deny.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> In March 2013, the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Security Council">Security Council</a> authorized the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Force_Intervention_Brigade" title="United Nations Force Intervention Brigade">United Nations Force Intervention Brigade</a> to neutralize armed groups.<sup id="cite_ref-UN1_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN1-69">[68]</a></sup> On 5 November 2013, M23 declared an end to its insurgency.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(6988913212).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg/220px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg/330px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg/440px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="833"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(6988913212).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>People fleeing their villages due to fighting between <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">FARDC</a> and rebel groups, <a href="/wiki/North_Kivu" title="North Kivu">North Kivu</a>, 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Additionally, in northern <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">Katanga</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mai-Mai" title="Mai-Mai">Mai-Mai</a> created by Laurent Kabila slipped out of the control of Kinshasa with <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9d%C3%A9on_Kyungu_Mutanga" class="mw-redirect" title="Gédéon Kyungu Mutanga">Gédéon Kyungu Mutanga</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mai_Mai_Kata_Katanga" class="mw-redirect" title="Mai Mai Kata Katanga">Mai Mai Kata Katanga</a> briefly invading the provincial capital of <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a> in 2013 and 400,000 persons displaced in the province as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> On and off fighting in the <a href="/wiki/Ituri_conflict" title="Ituri conflict">Ituri conflict</a> occurred between the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_and_Integrationist_Front" title="Nationalist and Integrationist Front">Nationalist and Integrationist Front</a> (FNI) and the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Congolese_Patriots" title="Union of Congolese Patriots">Union of Congolese Patriots</a> (UPC) who claimed to represent the <a href="/wiki/Lendu" class="mw-redirect" title="Lendu">Lendu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hema_people" title="Hema people">Hema</a> ethnic groups, respectively. In the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kony" title="Joseph Kony">Joseph Kony</a>'s <a href="/wiki/LRA" class="mw-redirect" title="LRA">LRA</a> moved from their original bases in Uganda and South Sudan to DR Congo in 2005 and set up camps in the Garamba National Park.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2009, <i>The New York Times</i> reported that people in the Congo continued to die at a rate of an estimated 45,000 per month<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup>&nbsp;– estimates of the number who have died from the long conflict range from 900,000 to 5,400,000.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> The death toll is due to widespread disease and famine; reports indicate that almost half of the individuals who have died are children under five years of age.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> There have been frequent reports of weapon bearers killing civilians, of the destruction of property, of widespread sexual violence,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> causing hundreds of thousands of people to flee their homes, and of other breaches of humanitarian and human rights law. One study found that more than <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">400,000 women are raped</a> in the Democratic Republic of Congo every year.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The war in the Congo has been described as the bloodiest war since World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> On 8 December 2017, fourteen UN soldiers and five Congolese regular soldiers were killed in a rebel attack at Semuliki in Beni territory. The rebels were thought to be <a href="/wiki/Allied_Democratic_Forces" title="Allied Democratic Forces">Allied Democratic Forces</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> UN investigations confirmed that aggressor in the December attack.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_(21_May_2013)_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._(8782972992).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg/220px-FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg/330px-FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg/440px-FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_(21_May_2013)_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._(8782972992).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Government troops near <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a> during the <a href="/wiki/M23_rebellion" title="M23 rebellion">M23 rebellion</a> in May 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the Human Rights Watch and the New York University-based Congo Research Group, armed troops in DRC's eastern Kivu region have killed over 1,900 civilians and kidnapped at least 3,300 people since June 2017 to June 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Kabila.27s_term_in_office_and_multiple_anti-government_protests"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kabila's_term_in_office_and_multiple_anti-government_protests">Kabila's term in office and multiple anti-government protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Kabila's term in office and multiple anti-government protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In 2015, <a href="/wiki/2015_Congolese_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 Congolese protests">major protests</a> broke out across the country and protesters demanded that Joseph Kabila step down as President. The protests began after the passage of a law by the Congolese lower house that, if also passed by the Congolese upper house, would keep Kabila in power at least until a national census was conducted (a process which would likely take several years and therefore keep him in power past the planned 2016 elections, which he is constitutionally barred from participating in). </p>
      <p>This bill passed; however, it was gutted of the provision that would keep Kabila in power until a census took place. A census is supposed to take place, but it is no longer tied to when the elections take place. In 2015, elections were scheduled for late 2016 and a tenuous peace held in the Congo.<sup id="cite_ref-The_DRC_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_DRC-83">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 27 November Congolese foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Tshibanda" title="Raymond Tshibanda">Raymond Tshibanda</a> told the press no elections would be held in 2016, after 20 December, the end of president Kabila's term. In a conference in Madagascar, Tshibanda said that Kabila's government had "consulted election experts" from Congo, the United Nations and elsewhere, and that "it has been decided that the voter registration operation will end on July 31, 2017, and that election will take place in April 2018."<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/December_2016_Congolese_protests" title="December 2016 Congolese protests">Protests broke out in the country on 20 December</a> when Kabila's term in office ended. Across the country, dozens of protesters were killed and hundreds were arrested. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewed_regional_violence">Renewed regional violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Renewed regional violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Ituri_conflict" title="Ituri conflict">Ituri conflict</a>
      </div> 
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/Jan_Egeland" title="Jan Egeland">Jan Egeland</a>, presently Secretary-General of the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Refugee_Council" title="Norwegian Refugee Council">Norwegian Refugee Council</a>, the situation in the DRC became much worse in 2016 and 2017 and is a major moral and humanitarian challenge comparable to the wars in Syria and Yemen, which receive much more attention. Women and children are abused sexually and "abused in all possible manners". Besides the conflict in <a href="/wiki/North_Kivu" title="North Kivu">North Kivu</a>, violence has gone up in the <a href="/wiki/Kasai_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Kasai region">Kasai region</a>. The armed groups are after <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a> to line the pockets of rich men both in the region and internationally. There are also ethnic and cultural rivalries at play, as well as religious motives and the political crisis with postponed elections. He says people believe the situation in the DRC is "stably bad" but in fact, it has become much, much worse. "The big wars of the Congo that were really on top of the agenda 15 years ago are back and worsening".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> Due to disruption of planting and harvesting caused by the conflict, the UN estimated in March 2018 that two million children risk starvation.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Human Rights Watch said in 2017 that Joseph Kabila recruited former <a href="/wiki/March_23_Movement" title="March 23 Movement">March 23 Movement</a> fighters to put down country-wide protests over his refusal to step down from office at the end of his term. "M23 fighters patrolled the streets of Congo's main cities, firing on or arresting protesters or anyone else deemed to be a threat to the president," they said.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Fierce fighting has erupted in Masisi between government forces and a powerful local warlord, General Delta. The United Nations mission in the DRC is its largest and most expensive peacekeeping effort, but it shut down five UN bases near Masisi in 2017, after the US led a push to cut costs.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_ethnic_conflict">2018 ethnic conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2018 ethnic conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2018_Yumbi_violence" title="2018 Yumbi violence">2018 Yumbi violence</a>
      </div> 
      <p>A tribal conflict erupted on 16–17 December 2018 at <a href="/wiki/Yumbi" title="Yumbi">Yumbi</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mai-Ndombe_Province" title="Mai-Ndombe Province">Mai-Ndombe Province</a>, 400&nbsp;km (250 miles) north of Kinshasa. Nearly 900 Banunu people from four villages were slaughtered by members of the Batende community in a deep-rooted rivalry over monthly tribal duties, land, fields and water resources. Some 100 Banunus fled to Moniende island in the Congo River, and another 16,000 to <a href="/wiki/Makotimpoko_District" title="Makotimpoko District">Makotimpoko District</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Congo">Republic of Congo</a>. Military-style tactics were employed in the bloodbath, and some assailants were clothed in army uniforms. Local authorities and elements within the security forces were suspected of lending them support.<sup id="cite_ref-afp1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afp1-89">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2018_election_and_new_president_.282018-Present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_election_and_new_president_(2018-Present)">2018 election and new president (2018-Present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2018 election and new president (2018-Present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg/220px-F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg/330px-F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg/440px-F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1723" data-file-height="1075"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>DR Congo's President <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi" title="Félix Tshisekedi">Félix Tshisekedi</a> with Congolese President <a href="/wiki/Denis_Sassou_Nguesso" title="Denis Sassou Nguesso">Denis Sassou Nguesso</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 30 December the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_general_election,_2018" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo general election, 2018">Democratic Republic of the Congo general election, 2018</a> was held. On 10 January 2019, the electoral commission announced opposition candidate <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi" title="Félix Tshisekedi">Félix Tshisekedi</a> as the winner of the presidential vote.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> He was officially sworn in as President on 24 January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-inaug_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inaug-91">[90]</a></sup> However, there were widespread suspicions that the results were rigged and that a deal had been made between Tshisekedi and Kabila. The Catholic Church said that the official results did not correspond to the information its election monitors had collected.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> The government had also "delayed" the vote until March in some areas, citing the <a href="/wiki/2018_Kivu_Ebola_outbreak" class="mw-redirect" title="2018 Kivu Ebola outbreak">Ebola outbreak in Kivu</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">the ongoing military conflict</a>. This was criticized as these regions are known as opposition strongholds.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> In August 2019, six months after the inauguration of Félix Tshisekedi, a coalition government was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A major <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a> outbreak in the country left nearly 5,000 dead in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> The 2018 Ebola outbreak ended in June 2020, which had caused 2,280 deaths over 2 years.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> Another, smaller Ebola outbreak in the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_%C3%89quateur" title="Province of Équateur">Équateur Province</a> began in June 2020, ultimately causing 55 deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Italian ambassador to the DRC, Luca Attanasio, and his bodyguard were <a href="/wiki/Killing_of_Luca_Attanasio" title="Killing of Luca Attanasio">killed in North Kivu on 22 February 2021</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The political allies of former president Joseph Kabila, who stepped down in January 2019, maintained control of key ministries, the legislature, judiciary and security services. However, President Felix Tshisekedi succeeded to strengthen his hold on power. In a series of moves, he won over more legislators, gaining the support of almost 400 out of 500 members of the National Assembly. The pro-Kabila speakers of both houses of parliament were forced out. In April 2021, the new government was formed without the supporters of Kabila.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A vaccination campaign against <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a> began on 19 April 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 22 April 2021, meetings between Kenyan President <a href="/wiki/Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Uhuru Kenyatta">Uhuru Kenyatta</a> and the DRC President Felix Tshisekedi resulted in new agreements increasing international trade and security (counterterrorism, immigration, cyber security, and customs) between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cg-map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cg-map.png/220px-Cg-map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Cg-map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="330" data-file-height="354"></a>

        </div>
