The DRC has more navigable rivers and moves more passengers and goods by boat and ferry than any other country in Africa, but air transport remains the only effective means of moving goods and people between many places within the country, especially in rural areas. Chronic economic mismanagement, political corruption and internal conflicts have led to long-term under-investment of infrastructure. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Rail transport in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Rail transport in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Train_rdc.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Train_rdc.svg/280px-Train_rdc.svg.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Train_rdc.svg/420px-Train_rdc.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Train_rdc.svg/560px-Train_rdc.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="671" data-file-height="559"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Train_rdc.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of rail network
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Rail transportation is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Railroad_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Congo Railroad Company">Congo Railroad Company</a> (Société Nationale des Chemins de Fer du Congo) and the <a href="/wiki/Office_National_des_Transports_(Congo)" class="mw-redirect" title="Office National des Transports (Congo)">Office National des Transports (Congo)</a> (ONATRA) and the Office of the Uele Railways (Office des Chemins de fer des Ueles, CFU). Like much of the infrastructure in the Congo, the railways are poorly maintained, dirty, crowded and dangerous. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo has fewer all-weather paved highways than any country of its population and size in Africa&nbsp;— a total of 2,250&nbsp;km (1,400&nbsp;mi), of which only 1,226&nbsp;km (762&nbsp;mi) is in good condition (see below). To put this in perspective, the road distance across the country in any direction is more than 2,500&nbsp;km (1,600&nbsp;mi) (e.g. Matadi to Lubumbashi, 2,700&nbsp;km (1,700&nbsp;mi) by road). The figure of 2,250&nbsp;km (1,400&nbsp;mi) converts to 35&nbsp;km (22&nbsp;mi) of paved road per 1,000,000 of population. Comparative figures for Zambia and Botswana are 721&nbsp;km (448&nbsp;mi) and 3,427&nbsp;km (2,129&nbsp;mi) respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Three routes in the <a href="/wiki/Trans-African_Highway_network" title="Trans-African Highway network">Trans-African Highway network</a> pass through DR Congo: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Tripoli-Cape_Town_Highway" class="mw-redirect" title="Tripoli-Cape Town Highway">Tripoli-Cape Town Highway</a>: this route crosses the western extremity of the country on National Road No. 1 between Kinshasa and <a href="/wiki/Matadi" title="Matadi">Matadi</a>, a distance of 285&nbsp;km (177&nbsp;mi) on one of the only paved sections in fair condition.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Lagos-Mombasa_Highway" class="mw-redirect" title="Lagos-Mombasa Highway">Lagos-Mombasa Highway</a>: the DR Congo is the main missing link in this east-west highway and requires a new road to be constructed before it can function.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Beira-Lobito_Highway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beira-Lobito Highway">Beira-Lobito Highway</a>: this east-west highway crosses <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">Katanga</a> and requires re-construction over most of its length, being an earth track between the Angolan border and <a href="/wiki/Kolwezi" title="Kolwezi">Kolwezi</a>, a paved road in very poor condition between Kolwezi and <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a>, and a paved road in fair condition over the short distance to the Zambian border.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The Democratic Republic of Congo has thousands of kilometres of <a href="/wiki/Navigable" class="mw-redirect" title="Navigable">navigable</a> <a href="/wiki/Waterway" title="Waterway">waterways</a>. Traditionally water transport has been the dominant means of moving around in approximately two-thirds of the country. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>As of June&nbsp;2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, DR Congo had one major national airline (<a href="/wiki/Congo_Airways" title="Congo Airways">Congo Airways</a>) that offered flights inside DR Congo. Congo Airways was based at <a href="/wiki/N%27djili_Airport" title="N'djili Airport">Kinshasa's international airport</a>. All air carriers certified by the DRC have been banned from European Union airports by the European Commission, due to inadequate safety standards.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Several international airlines service Kinshasa's international airport and a few also offer international flights to <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi_International_Airport" title="Lubumbashi International Airport">Lubumbashi International Airport</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the Democratic Republic of the Congo, there are both coal and <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> resources that were mainly used domestically in 2008. The Democratic Republic of Congo has the infrastructure for hydro-electricity from the Congo River at the <a href="/wiki/Inga_dams" title="Inga dams">Inga dams</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> The Democratic Republic of Congo also possesses 50% of Africa's forests and a river system that could provide <a href="/wiki/Hydro-electric" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydro-electric">hydro-electric</a> power to the entire continent, according to a UN report on the country's strategic significance and its potential role as an economic power in central Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The generation and distribution of electricity are controlled by <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_nationale_d%27%C3%A9lectricit%C3%A9_(SNEL)" class="mw-redirect" title="Société nationale d'électricité (SNEL)">Société nationale d'électricité (SNEL)</a>, but only 15% of the country has access to electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> The DRC is a member of three electrical power pools. These are SAPP (Southern African Power Pool), EAPP (East African Power Pool), CAPP (Central African Power Pool). </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewable_energy">Renewable energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Renewable energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewable energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Renewable energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Because of abundant sunlight, the potential for solar development is very high in the DRC. There are already about 836 solar power systems in the DRC, with a total power of 83&nbsp;kW, located in <a href="/wiki/Province_of_%C3%89quateur" title="Province of Équateur">Équateur</a> (167), Katanga (159), Nord-Kivu (170), the two Kasaï provinces (170), and Bas-Congo (170). Also, the 148 Caritas network system has a total power of 6.31&nbsp;kW.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Education in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Education in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:DRC_classroom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/DRC_classroom.jpg/220px-DRC_classroom.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/DRC_classroom.jpg/330px-DRC_classroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/DRC_classroom.jpg/440px-DRC_classroom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1197"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:DRC_classroom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A classroom in the Democratic Republic of the Congo.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate for the population between the ages of 15 and 49 was estimated to be 75.9% (88.1% male and 63.8% female) according to a <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">DHS</a> nationwide survey.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> The education system in the Democratic Republic of the Congo is governed by three government ministries: the <i>Ministère de l'Enseignement Primaire, Secondaire et Professionnel (MEPSP</i>), the <i>Ministère de l'Enseignement Supérieur et Universitaire (MESU)</i> and the <i>Ministère des Affaires Sociales (MAS)</i>. Primary education in the Democratic Republic of the Congo is not free or compulsory,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> even though the Congolese constitution says it should be (Article 43 of the 2005 Congolese Constitution).<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a result of the six-year civil war in the late 1990s—early 2000s, over 5.2&nbsp;million children in the country did not receive any education.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-182">[181]</a></sup> Since the end of the civil war, the situation has improved tremendously, with the number of children enrolled in primary schools rising from 5.5&nbsp;million in 2002 to 16.8&nbsp;million in 2018, and the number of children enrolled in secondary schools rising from 2.8&nbsp;million in 2007 to 4.6&nbsp;million in 2015 according to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Actual school attendance has also improved greatly in recent years, with primary school net attendance estimated to be 82.4% in 2014 (82.4% of children ages 6–11 attended school; 83.4% for boys, 80.6% for girls).<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Health in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Health in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="HIV/AIDS in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">HIV/AIDS in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="List of hospitals in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">hospitals in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa_General_Hospital" title="Kinshasa General Hospital">General Hospital of Kinshasa</a>. DRC has the world's second-highest rate of <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>). In April 2011, through aid from <a href="/wiki/GAVI_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="GAVI Alliance">Global Alliance for Vaccines</a>, a new vaccine to prevent <a href="/wiki/Pneumococcal_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Pneumococcal disease">pneumococcal disease</a> was introduced around Kinshasa.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2012, it was estimated that about 1.1% of adults aged 15–49 were living with <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> is also a problem.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">Yellow fever</a> also affects DRC.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Maternal_health" title="Maternal health">Maternal health</a> is poor in DRC. According to 2010 estimates, DRC has the 17th highest <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality">maternal mortality</a> rate in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>, 43.5% of children under five are <a href="/wiki/Stunted" class="mw-redirect" title="Stunted">stunted</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In May 2019, the death toll from the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Kivu_Ebola_epidemic" class="mw-redirect" title="2018–19 Kivu Ebola epidemic">Ebola outbreak</a> in DRC surpassed 1,000.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> emergency food relief agency warned that amid the escalating conflict and worsening situation following <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">COVID-19</a> in the Democratic Republic of Congo, millions of lives were at risk as they could die of hunger. According to the data of the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a>, four in ten people in Congo lack food security and about 15.6 million have been facing hunger crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime_and_law_enforcement">Crime and law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Crime and law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Crime in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Crime in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Congolese_National_Police" title="Congolese National Police">Congolese National Police</a> (PNC) are the primary police force in the Democratic Republic of the Congo.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Demographics of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Demographics of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Poverty in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Poverty in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage_in_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Child marriage in Democratic Republic of the Congo">Child marriage in Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div>

         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Masina,_Kinshasa" title="Masina, Kinshasa">Masina</a></td>

         <td style="text-align:right;">485,167 </td>
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kongo_people2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Kongo_people2.jpg/220px-Kongo_people2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Kongo_people2.jpg/330px-Kongo_people2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Kongo_people2.jpg/440px-Kongo_people2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kongo_people2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo</a> youth and adults in <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa, Democratic Republic of Congo</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Photo_of_the_Day,_17_February_2014_(12589890963).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg/220px-Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg/330px-Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg/440px-Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="1853"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Photo_of_the_Day,_17_February_2014_(12589890963).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Amani festival in <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg/220px-Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg/330px-Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg/440px-Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Family in Rutshuru, North Kivu, Democratic Republic of the Congo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Over 200 ethnic groups populate the Democratic Republic of the Congo, of which the majority are <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a>. Together, <a href="/wiki/Mongo_people" title="Mongo people">Mongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luba_people" title="Luba people">Luba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo</a> peoples, <a href="/wiki/Mangbetu_people" title="Mangbetu people">Mangbetu</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Zande_people" title="Zande people">Azande</a> peoples constitute around 45% of the population. The Kongo people are the largest ethnic group in the Democratic Republic of Congo.<sup id="cite_ref-Gates2010p14_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gates2010p14-196">[195]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, the United Nations estimated the country's population to be 84 million people,<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-197">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-198">[197]</a></sup> a rapid increase from 39.1&nbsp;million in 1992 despite the ongoing war.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> As many as 250 ethnic groups have been identified and named. The most numerous people are the Kongo, Luba, and Mongo. About 600,000 <a href="/wiki/Congo_Pygmies" class="mw-redirect" title="Congo Pygmies">Pygmies</a> are the aboriginal people of the DR Congo.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup> Although several hundred local languages and dialects are spoken, the linguistic variety is bridged both by widespread use of French and the national intermediary languages <a href="/wiki/Kongo_language" title="Kongo language">Kikongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tshiluba_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Tshiluba language">Tshiluba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lingala_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migration">Migration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Migration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(7134901927).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg/220px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg/330px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg/440px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="625"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(7134901927).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population fleeing their villages due to fighting between FARDC and rebels groups, Sake North Kivu 30 April 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Given the situation in the country and the condition of state structures, it is extremely difficult to obtain reliable migration data. However, evidence suggests that DRC continues to be a destination country for immigrants, in spite of recent declines in their numbers. Immigration is very diverse in nature; refugees and asylum-seekers&nbsp;– products of the numerous and violent conflicts in the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">Great Lakes Region</a>&nbsp;– constitute an important subset of the population. Additionally, the country's large mine operations attract migrant workers from Africa and beyond. There is also considerable migration for commercial activities from other African countries and the rest of the world, but these movements are not well studied.<sup id="cite_ref-IOMProfile_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IOMProfile-201">[200]</a></sup> Transit migration towards South Africa and Europe also plays a role. </p>
      <p>Immigration to the DRC has decreased steadily over the past two decades, most likely as a result of the armed violence that the country has experienced. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a>, the number of immigrants in the DRC has fallen from just over one million in 1960, to 754,000 in 1990, to 480,000 in 2005, to an estimated 445,000 in 2010. Official figures are unavailable, partly due to the predominance of the <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">informal economy</a> in the DRC. Data are also lacking on irregular immigrants, however given neighbouring countries' ethnic links to DRC nationals, irregular migration is assumed to be a significant phenomenon.<sup id="cite_ref-IOMProfile_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IOMProfile-201">[200]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Figures for Congolese nationals abroad vary greatly depending on the source, from three to six million. This discrepancy is due to a lack of official, reliable data. Emigrants from the DRC are above all long-term emigrants, the majority of whom live in Africa and to a lesser extent in Europe; 79.7% and 15.3% respectively, according to estimated 2000 data. New destination countries include South Africa and various points en route to Europe. The DRC has produced a considerable number of <a href="/wiki/Refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Refugees">refugees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asylum-seekers" class="mw-redirect" title="Asylum-seekers">asylum-seekers</a> located in the region and beyond. These numbers peaked in 2004 when, according to <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a>, there were more than 460,000 refugees from the DRC; in 2008, Congolese refugees numbered 367,995 in total, 68% of whom were living in other African countries.<sup id="cite_ref-IOMProfile_201-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IOMProfile-201">[200]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 2003, more than 400,000 Congolese migrants have been expelled from <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Religion in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Religion in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Population_pyramid_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Population_pyramid_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo.jpg/220px-Population_pyramid_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Population_pyramid_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo.jpg/330px-Population_pyramid_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Population_pyramid_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo.jpg/440px-Population_pyramid_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Population_pyramid_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The population pyramid of the Democratic Republic of the Congo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Christianity is the majority religion in the Democratic Republic of the Congo. The most recent survey, conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> Program in 2013–2014 indicated that Christians constituted 93.7% of the population (with Catholics making up 29.7%, Protestants 26.8%, and other Christians 37.2%). An indigenous Christian religious movement, <a href="/wiki/Kimbanguism" title="Kimbanguism">Kimbanguism</a>, had the adherence of only 2.8%, while Muslims made up 1.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_2013-14_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_2013-14-203">[202]</a></sup> Other recent estimates have found Christianity the majority religion, followed by 95.8% of the population according to a 2010 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a><sup id="cite_ref-religion_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion-204">[203]</a></sup> estimate, while the <a href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a> reports this figure to be 95.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup> The proportion of followers of Islam is variously estimated from 1%<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup> to 12% <sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are about 35&nbsp;million Catholics in the country<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-4">[3]</a></sup> with six <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese">archdioceses</a> and 41 <a href="/wiki/Dioceses" class="mw-redirect" title="Dioceses">dioceses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> The impact of the Catholic Church in the Democratic Republic of Congo is difficult to overestimate. Schatzberg has called it the country's "only truly national institution apart from the state."<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup> Its schools have educated over 60% of the nation's primary school students and more than 40% of its secondary students. The church owns and manages an extensive network of hospitals, schools, and clinics, as well as many diocesan economic enterprises, including farms, ranches, stores, and artisans' shops.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png/220px-Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png/330px-Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png/440px-Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2178"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Peace_Cathedral,_Bukavu" title="Our Lady of Peace Cathedral, Bukavu">Our Lady of Peace Cathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bukavu" title="Bukavu">Bukavu</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sixty-two Protestant denominations are federated under the umbrella of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Christ_in_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Church of Christ in Congo">Church of Christ in Congo</a>. It is often simply referred to as <i>the Protestant Church</i>, since it covers most of the DRC Protestants. With more than 25&nbsp;million members, it constitutes <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_Protestant_churches" class="mw-redirect" title="List of the largest Protestant churches">one of the largest Protestant bodies</a> in the world. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kimbanguism" title="Kimbanguism">Kimbanguism</a> was seen as a threat to the colonial regime and was banned by the Belgians. Kimbanguism, officially "the church of Christ on Earth by the prophet Simon Kimbangu", now has about three million members,<sup id="cite_ref-Adherents_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adherents-210">[209]</a></sup> primarily among the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Bakongo</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bas-Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Bas-Congo">Bas-Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> has been present in the Democratic Republic of the Congo since the 18th century, when Arab traders from <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a> pushed into the interior for <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a>- and slave-trading purposes. Today, Muslims constitute approximately 1% of the Congolese population according to Pew research center. The majority are <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> Muslims. </p>
      <p>The first members of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a> to live in the country came from Uganda in 1953. Four years later the first local administrative council was elected. In 1970 the National Spiritual Assembly (national administrative council) was first elected. Though the religion was banned in the 1970s and 1980s, due to misrepresentations of foreign governments, the ban was lifted by the end of the 1980s. In 2012 plans were announced to build a national <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_House_of_Worship" title="Baháʼí House of Worship">Baháʼí House of Worship</a> in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Traditional religions embody such concepts as <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">monotheism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitalism" title="Vitalism">vitalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spirit_worship" class="mw-redirect" title="Spirit worship">spirit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancestor_worship" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancestor worship">ancestor worship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a>, and sorcery and vary widely among ethnic groups. The syncretic sects often merge elements of Christianity with traditional beliefs and rituals and are not recognized by mainstream churches as part of Christianity. New variants of ancient beliefs have become widespread, led by US-inspired Pentecostal churches which have been in the forefront of witchcraft accusations, particularly against children and the elderly.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="What is the new belief? Witchcraft, or the accusations of witchcraft? (January 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> Children accused of witchcraft are sent away from homes and family, often to live on the street, which can lead to physical violence against these children.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="What leads to violence? (January 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> There are charities supporting street children such as the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Children_Trust" title="Congo Children Trust">Congo Children Trust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Congo_Children_Trust" title="Congo Children Trust">Congo Children Trust</a>'s flagship project is Kimbilio,<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[215]</a></sup> which works to reunite street children in <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a>. The usual term for these children is <i>enfants sorciers</i> (child witches) or <i>enfants dits sorciers</i> (children accused of witchcraft). Non-denominational church organizations have been formed to capitalize on this belief by charging exorbitant fees for <a href="/wiki/Exorcisms" class="mw-redirect" title="Exorcisms">exorcisms</a>. Though recently outlawed, children have been subjected in these exorcisms to often-violent abuse at the hands of self-proclaimed prophets and priests.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[216]</a></sup> </p>

         <td>2.1%</td> 
         <td>5.1%</td> 
         <td><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.thearda.com/internationalData/countries/Country_57_1.asp">[5]</a> </td>
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_-_DR_Congo,_major_languages.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg/220px-Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg/330px-Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg/440px-Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="729" data-file-height="679"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_-_DR_Congo,_major_languages.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Major Bantu languages in the Congo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Languages of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Languages of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>French is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of the Democratic Republic of the Congo. It is culturally accepted as the <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> facilitating communication among the many different ethnic groups of the Congo. According to a 2014 <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">OIF</a> report, 33&nbsp;million Congolese people (47% of the population) could read and write in French.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup> In the capital city <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>, 67% of the population could read and write French, and 68.5% could speak and understand it.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Approximately 242 languages are spoken in the country, but only four have the status of national languages: <a href="/wiki/Kituba_language" title="Kituba language">Kituba</a> ("Kikongo ya leta"), <a href="/wiki/Lingala_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tshiluba_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Tshiluba language">Tshiluba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>. Although some people speak these regional, or trade languages as first languages, most of the population speak them as a second language after their own ethnic language. Lingala was the official language of the colonial army, the "<a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a>", under Belgian colonial rule, and remains to this day the predominant language in the armed forces. Since the recent rebellions, a good part of the army in the East also uses Swahili where it is prevalent. </p>
      <p>When the country was a Belgian colony, the Belgian colonizers instituted teaching and use of the four national languages in primary schools, making it one of the few African nations to have had literacy in local languages during the European colonial period. This trend was reversed after independence, when French became the sole language of education at all levels.<sup id="cite_ref-lang_educ_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lang_educ-220">[219]</a></sup> Since 1975, the four national languages have been reintroduced in the first two years of primary education, with French becoming the sole language of education from the third year onward, but in practice many primary schools in urban areas solely use French from the first year of school onward.<sup id="cite_ref-lang_educ_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lang_educ-220">[219]</a></sup> Portuguese is taught in the Congolese schools as a foreign language. The lexical similarity and phonology with French makes Portuguese a relatively easy language for the people to learn. Most of the roughly 175,000 Portuguese speakers in the DRC are Angolan and Mozambican expatriates. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Culture of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Culture of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hemba_male_figure1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hemba_male_figure1.jpg/170px-Hemba_male_figure1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hemba_male_figure1.jpg/255px-Hemba_male_figure1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hemba_male_figure1.jpg/340px-Hemba_male_figure1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="853" data-file-height="1280"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hemba_male_figure1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Hemba" class="mw-redirect" title="Hemba">Hemba</a> male statue
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The culture of the Democratic Republic of the Congo reflects the diversity of its hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a> and their differing ways of life throughout the country&nbsp;&nbsp;— from the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">River Congo</a> on the coast, upriver through the <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> in its centre, to the more densely populated mountains in the far east. Since the late 19th century, traditional ways of life have undergone changes brought about by <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>, the struggle for independence, the stagnation of the Mobutu era, and most recently, the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo Wars</a>. Despite these pressures, the <a href="/wiki/Convention_(norm)" title="Convention (norm)">customs</a> and cultures of the Congo have retained much of their individuality. The country's 81&nbsp;million inhabitants (2016) are mainly rural. The 30% who live in urban areas have been the most open to <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western</a> influences. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Another feature in Congo culture is its music. The DRC has its influences on Cuban music <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Rumba" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban Rumba">rumba</a>, originally kumba from Congo and <a href="/wiki/Merengue_music" title="Merengue music">merengue</a>. And those two later give birth to <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">soukous</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[220]</a></sup> Other African nations produce music genres derived from Congolese soukous. Some of the African bands sing in <a href="/wiki/Lingala" title="Lingala">Lingala</a>, one of the main languages in the DRC. The same Congolese soukous, under the guidance of "le sapeur", <a href="/wiki/Papa_Wemba" title="Papa Wemba">Papa Wemba</a>, have set the tone for a generation of young men always dressed up in expensive designer clothes. They came to be known as the fourth generation of Congolese music and mostly come from the former well-known band <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wenge_Musica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wenge Musica (page does not exist)">Wenge Musica</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wenge_Musica" class="extiw" title="fr:Wenge Musica">fr</a>]</span>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sport_in_DR_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sport in DR Congo (page does not exist)">Sport in DR Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_(8756673901).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg/220px-Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg/330px-Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg/440px-Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3787" data-file-height="2074"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_(8756673901).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Stade_des_Martyrs" title="Stade des Martyrs">Stade des Martyrs</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Many sports are played in the Democratic Republic of the Congo, including <a href="/wiki/Football_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Football in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">football</a>, basketball, and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Rugby union in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">rugby</a>. The sports are played in numerous stadiums throughout the country, including the <a href="/wiki/Stade_Frederic_Kibassa_Maliba" title="Stade Frederic Kibassa Maliba">Stade Frederic Kibassa Maliba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[221]</a></sup> As Zaire they have participated in the World Cup Football (Final stage) in 1974. </p>
      <p>Internationally, the country is especially famous for its professional basketball <a href="/wiki/NBA" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA">NBA</a> and football players. <a href="/wiki/Dikembe_Mutombo" title="Dikembe Mutombo">Dikembe Mutombo</a> is one of the best African basketball players to ever play the game. Mutombo is well known for humanitarian projects in his home country. <a href="/wiki/Bismack_Biyombo" title="Bismack Biyombo">Bismack Biyombo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Eyenga" title="Christian Eyenga">Christian Eyenga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Mudiay" title="Emmanuel Mudiay">Emmanuel Mudiay</a> are others who gained significant international attention in basketball. Several Congolese players and players of Congolese descent—including strikers <a href="/wiki/Romelu_Lukaku" title="Romelu Lukaku">Romelu Lukaku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yannick_Bolasie" title="Yannick Bolasie">Yannick Bolasie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dieumerci_Mbokani" title="Dieumerci Mbokani">Dieumerci Mbokani</a>—have gained prominence in world football. DR Congo has twice won the African Cup of Nations football tournament. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Congolese_cuisine" title="Congolese cuisine">Congolese cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Media of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Newspapers of the DRC include <i><a href="/wiki/L%27Avenir_(newspaper)" title="L'Avenir (newspaper)">L'Avenir</a></i>, <i>Radion Télévision Mwangaza</i>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=La_Conscience&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="La Conscience (page does not exist)">La Conscience</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Conscience" class="extiw" title="fr:La Conscience">fr</a>]</span></i>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=L%27Observateur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="L'Observateur (page does not exist)">L'Observateur</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/L%27Observateur_(RDC)" class="extiw" title="fr:L'Observateur (RDC)">fr</a>]</span></i>, <i>Le Phare</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Potentiel" title="Le Potentiel">Le Potentiel</a></i>, <i>Le Soft</i> and <i>LeCongolais.CD</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup> a web-based daily.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup> Radio Télévision Nationale Congolaise (RTNC) is the national broadcaster of the Democratic Republic of the Congo. RTNC currently broadcasts in <a href="/wiki/Lingala_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a>, French, and English. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/List_of_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_writers" title="List of Democratic Republic of the Congo writers">Congolese authors</a> use literature as a way to develop a sense of <a href="/wiki/National_consciousness" class="mw-redirect" title="National consciousness">national consciousness</a> amongst the Congo people. The tragic history of colonialism and <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">war</a> lead the Congolese people to settle in a place of complacency, accepting the culture that was forced upon them by <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgium</a>. </p>
      <p>Modern Congolese literature began to emerge in the late 1950s. There are a few rare pieces of literature dated back to before <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_I)" class="mw-redirect" title="East African Campaign (World War I)">WWI</a>, but it was not until about 1954 that literature written in French made its appearance in the Congo. After gaining their independence from Belgium in the 1960s, new authors, such as Guy Menga and Jean Pierre Makouta-Mboukou, were inspired by older authors, such as <a href="/wiki/Jean_Malonga" title="Jean Malonga">Jean Malonga</a> from Congo-Brazzaville, and used writing to bring attention to new issues affecting the Congo. The rise of female authors began in the 1970s introducing diversity to Congolese literature and support for gender empowerment. Many authors who have contributed to the success of Congolese literature are now living abroad due to economic and political issues.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Kambemba_Yamusangie" title="Frederick Kambemba Yamusangie">Frederick Kambemba Yamusangie</a> writes literature for the between generations of those who grew up in the Congo, during the time when they were colonised, fighting for independence and after. Yamusangie in an interview<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup> said he felt the distance in literature and wanted to remedy that he wrote the novel, Full Circle, which is a story of a boy named Emanuel who in the beginning of the book feels a difference in culture among the different groups in the Congo and elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%AFs_Neza_Boneza" title="Raïs Neza Boneza">Rais Neza Boneza</a>, an author from the <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">Katanga province</a> of the Democratic Republic of Congo, wrote novels and poems to promote artistic expressions as a way to address and deal with conflicts.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>These authors, along with others, used their platforms to bring awareness to the crises and conflicts that took place in the Congo. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>A dense <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforest</a> in the DRC's central <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">river basin</a> and eastern highlands is bordered on the east by the <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift" title="Albertine Rift">Albertine Rift</a> (the western branch of Africa's <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley" title="Great Rift Valley">Great Rift System</a>). It includes several of Africa's Great Lakes. </p>
      <p><b>Major environmental issues</b> </p>
      <p>DR Congo's major environmental issues include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a></li> 
       <li>poaching, which threatens wildlife populations</li> 
       <li>water pollution</li> 
       <li>mining</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Displaced refugees cause or are otherwise responsible for significant deforestation, soil erosion and wildlife poaching. Another significant issue is environmental damage from the mining of minerals, especially diamonds, gold, and <a href="/wiki/Coltan" title="Coltan">coltan</a> – a mineral used to manufacture <a href="/wiki/Capacitors" class="mw-redirect" title="Capacitors">capacitors</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Species_and_Biodiversity_loss">Species and Biodiversity loss</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Species and Biodiversity loss">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_loss" title="Biodiversity loss">biodiversity loss</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mountain_gorilla_(Gorilla_beringei_beringei)_yawn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg/220px-Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg/330px-Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg/440px-Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2952" data-file-height="2952"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mountain_gorilla_(Gorilla_beringei_beringei)_yawn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The endangered mountain gorilla, half of its population live in the DRC's <a href="/wiki/Virunga_National_Park" title="Virunga National Park">Virunga National Park</a>, making the park a critical habitat for these animals.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The environmental problems associated with The Democratic Republic of Congo (DRC) affect its many endemic species of flora and fauna. The DRC has the world's second largest contiguous rain forest after the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon</a> as well as other ecosystems including Savanna, swamps and flood plains. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a>, these unique habitats and species make the DRC one of the most valuable yet vulnerable areas in the world for biodiversity, wildlife protection and rainforest sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[229]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Species loss has been cited as a problem in the DRC, brought about or exacerbated by reasons that include deforestation for mining, wood fuel, infrastructure or agriculture, war, illegal poaching and increased consumption of bush meat due to overpopulation and lack of food security.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[230]</a></sup> Some attempts to combat species loss in countries such as the DRC are actions such as the UN's Sustainable Development Goals (SDG), specifically <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_15" title="Sustainable Development Goal 15">SDG 15</a> Life on Land, the primary goals of which is to increase reforestation and biodiversity and reduce species loss, desertification, and illegal poaching.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[231]</a></sup> One of the primary defences for species and habitat protection in the DRC is its system of national parks and reserves, which gives protected status to nearly 12% of the DRC's rainforest.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-233">[232]</a></sup> Five of these parks and reserves are <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_world_heritage" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO world heritage">UNESCO world heritage</a> sites, including Africa’s first national park <a href="/wiki/Virunga_National_Park" title="Virunga National Park">Virunga national park</a>. All of these parks have been put on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_in_Danger" title="List of World Heritage in Danger">World Heritage in Danger List</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup> Poor governance and low economic conditions have reduced the effectiveness of these protections, especially during war times.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-233">[232]</a></sup> The human cost of protecting these parks has also been high with 200 park ranger deaths in the past 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Virunga_National_Park" title="Virunga National Park">Virunga national park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salonga_National_Park" title="Salonga National Park">Salongo National Park</a>, both of which are <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> world heritage sites are currently being looked at for mining and oil exploration. The move would open 21.5% of the Virunga park for exploitation, this is highly criticised by animal rights activists as it would threaten the habitat of <a href="/wiki/Mountain_gorilla" title="Mountain gorilla">mountain gorillas</a> and other endangered species. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Deforestation">Deforestation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Deforestation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Deforestation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Deforestation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Changing_land_use_in_the_Masisi_-_Julien_Harneis_-_May_2_2007_-_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Changing_land_use_in_the_Masisi_-_Julien_Harneis_-_May_2_2007_-_4.jpg/220px-Changing_land_use_in_the_Masisi_-_Julien_Harneis_-_May_2_2007_-_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Changing_land_use_in_the_Masisi_-_Julien_Harneis_-_May_2_2007_-_4.jpg/330px-Changing_land_use_in_the_Masisi_-_Julien_Harneis_-_May_2_2007_-_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Changing_land_use_in_the_Masisi_-_Julien_Harneis_-_May_2_2007_-_4.jpg/440px-Changing_land_use_in_the_Masisi_-_Julien_Harneis_-_May_2_2007_-_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Changing_land_use_in_the_Masisi_-_Julien_Harneis_-_May_2_2007_-_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Deforested lands in the DRC
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Between 2000 and 2014 the DRC lost an average of 570,000 hectares (0.2%) of rainforest to deforestation per year, with the highest amount of deforestation coming between 2011 and 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup> Deforestation is the primary cause of biodiversity reduction and species loss globally, through habitat loss and fragmentation.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup> One of the goals of the SDG 15 is to reduce deforestation and encourage reforestation by 2020. The DRC had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.56/10, ranking it 36th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-238">[237]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The DRC has Africa’s largest rainforest, which is under the threat of deforestation through mining operations, agriculture, infrastructure and wood fuel. In the DRC 94% of wood taken from the rainforest is used for wood fuel, mainly due to poverty, lack of energy infrastructure and the decentralised nature of its population. To mitigate this aid agencies have tried to promote agro-forestry with fast growing trees to avoid over exploitation of the rainforests.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> Other large drivers of deforestation include mining and conflict, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Congo conflict</a> deforestation by militia groups was high for wood fuel, small mining operations and illegal logging to fund their operations. However, conversely conflict reduced deforestation for large scale mining due to security instability.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_233-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-233">[232]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>One policy being attempted to reduce the deforestation and increase biodiversity in the DRC is the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_REDD_Programme" title="United Nations REDD Programme">UN-REDD</a> program, which uses emissions trading system so that developed nations can offset their carbon emissions by paying developing nations with rainforest to manage and conserve their forest.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[239]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bush_meat">Bush meat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Bush meat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Bush meat refers to any meat that is procured from the wild. Overpopulation and continual conflicts in the DRC have led to food shortages, which have therefore increased the use of bush meat. Although, data on bush meat use is not extensive, studies estimate 6&nbsp;million tonnes of animals are taken for bush meat globally each year.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-241">[240]</a></sup> What animals are hunted are done so indiscriminately without thought of the importance of certain species that could be <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_engineer" title="Ecosystem engineer">ecosystem engineers</a> or <a href="/wiki/Keystone_species" title="Keystone species">keystone species</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-241">[240]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bush meat is an important source of protein for millions in the DRC, especially in rural areas where it makes up 50–70% of meals. For some who cannot afford farmed produce it is a free meal.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[241]</a></sup> A recent study in the DRC revealed that almost all of the animals are taken from the Congo each year, at 93% of all live animals there are in the forest are extracted for bush meat, whereas a sustainable rate would be 20%.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-243">[242]</a></sup> This is a huge amount compared to the Amazon where bush meat is hunted at only 3% the rate of the Congo.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-243">[242]</a></sup> the study reveals the only way to solve this is to find other food sources to feed people in the Congo Basin as bush meat is their only means of eating.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_243-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-243">[242]</a></sup> Another study showed that the species of bush meat in the meat markets of the DRC's third largest city <a href="/wiki/Kisangani" title="Kisangani">Kisangani</a> were primarily <a href="/wiki/Even-toed_ungulate" title="Even-toed ungulate">Artiodactyla</a> at 40.06% of the carcasses sold then <a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">primates</a> at 37.79% of carcasses sold.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[243]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Recently the prevalence of hunting for bush meat has declined because of the risk to hunters and butchers from the <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebola virus disease">Ebola virus</a> from specifically ape and bat meat.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-245">[244]</a></sup> Even though when the meat is cooked smoked or dried it kills the virus, business has dropped significantly with some hunters reporting as much of a reduction in sales of 80%.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_245-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-245">[244]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflicts">Conflicts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Conflicts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>There has been a war in the DRC in different levels of intensity since 1994 when the country was called <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-246">[245]</a></sup> Although what was known as <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Africa's World War</a> had ended in 2003 the eastern part of the country still has ongoing skirmishes between rebel groups and government forces.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-246">[245]</a></sup> No other method has reduced species population so dramatically than conflict, when a militia reached the <a href="/wiki/Garamba_National_Park" title="Garamba National Park">Garamba National Park</a> in 1997, within three months half of the park's elephants, two thirds of the buffalo, and three quarters of its hippos vanished.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-247">[246]</a></sup> The reason conflict is so damaging to wildlife is the increased use of bush meat to feed soldiers, the prevalence of weapons, the lucrative industry of selling exotic animals and ivory as well as the general failure of law and order.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_247-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-247">[246]</a></sup> According to another study which was taken during the time of the civil war in the <a href="/wiki/Okapi_Wildlife_Reserve" title="Okapi Wildlife Reserve">Okapi Faunal Reserve</a>, there was a 50% reduction in the abundance of elephants and a vast change in the distribution of them to the more secluded areas of the park.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[247]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Kikongo" here is actually referring to the Kituba language – which is known as <i>Kikongo ya leta</i> by its speakers – not the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_language" title="Kongo language">Kongo language</a> proper. The confusion arises from the fact that the government of the DRC officially recognizes and refers to the language simply as "Kikongo".</span> </li>

         <li id="cite_note-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-143">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The law on sexual violence, DRC 2006 (Les lois sur les violences sexuelles) reads (in French): <i>"Article 3, Paragraphe 7: De la mutilation sexuelle; Article 174g; Sera puni d’une peine de servitude pénale de deux à cinq ans et d’une amende de deux cent mille francs congolais constants, quiconque aura posé un acte qui porte atteinte à l’intégrité physique ou fonctionnelle des organes génitaux d’une personne. Lorsque la mutilation a entraîné la mort, la peine est de servitude pénale à perpétuité."</i>
